Stockholder: </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">You are cordially invited to attend the 2019 Annual Meeting of Stockholders (the &#147;Meeting&#148;) of Goldman Sachs BDC,
Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;) to be held on Friday, May&nbsp;17, 2019, at 10:00 a.m. (Eastern time), at the offices of Goldman Sachs Asset Management, L.P., located at 30 Hudson Street, Jersey City, New Jersey 07302. Please note that if you plan to
attend the Meeting in person, photographic identification will be required for admission. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>The Meeting is being held (i)&nbsp;to elect
two Class&nbsp;II directors of the Company, who will each serve until the 2022 annual meeting of stockholders or until his or her successor is duly elected and qualified, and (ii)&nbsp;to ratify the selection of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP as the
Company&#146;s independent registered public accounting firm for the fiscal year ending December&nbsp;31, 2019. </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">A formal Notice of
Annual Meeting and Proxy Statement setting forth in detail the matters to come before the Meeting are attached hereto, and a proxy card is enclosed for your use. You should read the Proxy Statement carefully. You will also receive separate proxy
materials for the 2019 Special Meeting of Stockholders, which will be held on the same date and at the same location as the Meeting. Please be certain to vote each proxy card that you receive from us. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>WHETHER OR NOT YOU PLAN TO BE PRESENT AT THE MEETING, YOUR VOTE IS VERY IMPORTANT. </B>If you do not plan to be present in person at the
Meeting, you can vote by signing, dating and returning the enclosed proxy card promptly or by using the Internet or telephone voting options as described on your proxy card. If you have any questions regarding the proxy materials, please contact the
Company at (866) <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">438-2987.</FONT> Your prompt response will help reduce proxy costs&#151;which are paid by the Company and indirectly by its stockholders&#151;and will also mean that you can avoid receiving <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">follow-up</FONT> phone calls and mailings. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:54%; text-indent:-2%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sincerely, </P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>To Be Held On Friday, May&nbsp;17, 2019 </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right">April&nbsp;1, 2019 </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Notice is
hereby given to the owners of shares of common stock (the &#147;Stockholders&#148;) of Goldman Sachs BDC, Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;) that: </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The 2019 Annual Meeting of Stockholders (the &#147;Meeting&#148;) will be held on Friday, May&nbsp;17, 2019, at 10:00&nbsp;a.m.&nbsp;(Eastern
time), at the offices of Goldman Sachs Asset Management, L.P. (&#147;GSAM&#148;), located at 30&nbsp;Hudson Street, Jersey City, New Jersey 07302, for the following purposes (the &#147;Proposals&#148;): </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="4%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><B>1.</B></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left"><B>to elect two Class&nbsp;II directors of the Company, who will each serve until the 2022 annual meeting of
the stockholders or until his or her successor is duly elected and qualified; and </B></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left"><B>to ratify the selection of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP as the Company&#146;s independent registered public
accounting firm for the fiscal year ending December&nbsp;31, 2019. </B></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The matters referred to above are discussed in
the Proxy Statement attached to this Notice. On February&nbsp;27, 2019, the Board of Directors of the Company, including each of the independent directors, unanimously recommended that you vote <B>&#147;FOR&#148; </B>each of the Proposals. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Stockholders of record at the close of business on Monday, March&nbsp;18, 2019 are entitled to receive notice of, and to vote at, the Meeting
and at any postponements or adjournments thereof. Each Stockholder is invited to attend the Meeting in person. Please note that if you plan to attend the Meeting in person, photographic identification will be required for admission. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Your vote is extremely important to us. If you will not attend the Meeting in person, we urge you to sign, date and promptly return the
enclosed proxy card in the envelope provided, which is addressed for your convenience and needs no postage if mailed in the United States. You may also vote easily and quickly by Internet or by telephone. In the event there are not sufficient votes
for a quorum or to approve the Proposals at the time of the Meeting, the Meeting may be postponed or adjourned in order to permit further solicitation of proxies by the Board of Directors of the Company. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:54%; text-indent:-2%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">By Order of the Board of Directors </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:54%; text-indent:-2%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">of Goldman Sachs BDC, Inc. </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>YOUR VOTE IS IMPORTANT</B> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>NO MATTER HOW MANY SHARES YOU OWN </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">To secure the largest possible representation at the Meeting, please mark your proxy card, sign it, date it, and return it in the postage-paid
envelope provided (unless you are voting by Internet or by telephone). <B>If you sign, date and return a proxy card but give no voting instructions, your shares will be voted &#147;FOR&#148; all of the proposals indicated on the card. </B>If you
prefer, you may instead vote via the Internet or by telephone. To vote in this manner, you should refer to the directions below. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">To vote
via the Internet, please access the website found on your proxy card and follow the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">on-screen</FONT> <B>instructions</B> on the website. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">To vote by telephone, Stockholders within the United States should call the toll-free number found on the proxy card and follow the recorded
instructions. Stockholders outside the United States should vote via the Internet or by submitting a proxy card instead. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">You may revoke
your proxy at any time at or before the Meeting (1)&nbsp;by notifying the Secretary of the Company in writing at the Company&#146;s principal executive offices, (2)&nbsp;by submitting a properly executed, later-dated proxy or (3)&nbsp;by attending
the Meeting and voting in person. </P>

York, New York 10282 </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>PROXY STATEMENT </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right">April&nbsp;1, 2019 </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This Proxy
Statement is furnished in connection with the solicitation of proxies by and on behalf of the Board of Directors (the &#147;Board&#148;) of Goldman Sachs BDC, Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;) for use at the 2019 Annual Meeting of Stockholders (the
&#147;Meeting&#148;), to be held at the offices of Goldman Sachs Asset Management, L.P. (&#147;GSAM&#148;), located at 30 Hudson Street, Jersey City, New Jersey 07302, on Friday, May&nbsp;17, 2019, at 10:00 a.m. (Eastern time), and any postponement
or adjournment thereof. Much of the information in this Proxy Statement is required under rules of the Securities and Exchange Commission (the &#147;SEC&#148;), and some of it is technical in nature. If there is anything you do not understand,
please contact the Company at (866) <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">438-2987.</FONT> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This Proxy Statement, the accompanying Notice of
Annual Meeting and proxy card and the Company&#146;s Annual Report on Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-K</FONT> for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018 are being mailed to stockholders (the &#147;Stockholders&#148;) of the Company of
record as of Monday, March&nbsp;18, 2019 (the &#147;Record Date&#148;) on or about March&nbsp;22, 2019. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>PURPOSE OF THE MEETING </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">At the Meeting, you will be asked to vote on the following proposals: </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">1.</TD>

stockholders or until his or her successor is duly elected and qualified (&#147;Proposal 1&#148;); and </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

accounting firm for the fiscal year ending December&nbsp;31, 2019 (&#147;Proposal 2&#148;). </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>INFORMATION REGARDING
THIS SOLICITATION </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">It is expected that the solicitation of proxies will be primarily by mail. The Company&#146;s officers, and
personnel of the Company&#146;s investment adviser, GSAM, and the Company&#146;s transfer agent and any authorized proxy solicitation agent, may also solicit proxies by telephone, email, facsimile, Internet or in person. If the Company records votes
through the Internet or by telephone, it will use procedures designed to authenticate Stockholders&#146; identities to allow Stockholders to authorize the voting of their shares in accordance with their instructions and to confirm that their
identities have been properly recorded. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company will pay the expenses associated with this Proxy Statement and solicitation, in a
manner agreed upon by the Board. The Company has engaged Computershare Inc. and Broadridge Financial Services, </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">1 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
Inc. to assist in the distribution of the proxy materials and tabulation of proxies. The cost of such services with respect to the Company is estimated to be approximately $60,000, plus
reasonable <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">out-of-pocket</FONT></FONT> expenses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">To vote by mail, sign,
date and promptly return the enclosed proxy card in the accompanying postage <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-paid</FONT> envelope. To vote by Internet or telephone, please use the control number on your proxy card and follow the instructions as
described on your proxy card. If you have any questions regarding the proxy materials, please contact the Company at (866) <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">438-2987.</FONT> <B>If the enclosed proxy card is properly executed and received prior to the
Meeting and has not been revoked, the shares represented thereby will be voted in accordance with the instructions marked on the returned proxy card or, if no instructions are marked, the proxy card will be voted &#147;FOR&#148; each of the
Proposals described in this Proxy Statement; and in the discretion of the persons named as proxies in connection with any other matter that may properly come before the Meeting or any adjournment(s) or postponement(s) thereof.</B> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Any person giving a proxy may revoke it at any time before it is exercised (1)&nbsp;by notifying the Secretary of the Company in writing at
the Company&#146;s principal executive offices, (2)&nbsp;by submitting a properly executed, later-dated proxy or (3)&nbsp;by attending the Meeting and voting in person. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">If (i)&nbsp;you are a member of a household in which multiple Stockholders share the same address, (ii)&nbsp;your shares are held in
&#147;street name&#148; and (iii)&nbsp;your broker or bank has received consent to household material, then your broker or bank may send to your household only one copy of this Proxy Statement, unless your broker or bank previously received contrary
instructions from a Stockholder in your household. If you are part of a household that has received only one copy of this Proxy Statement, the Company will deliver promptly a separate copy of this Proxy Statement to you upon written or oral request.
To receive a separate copy of this Proxy Statement, please contact the Company by calling (toll-free) (866) <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">438-2987</FONT> or by mail to the Company&#146;s principal executive offices at Goldman Sachs BDC, Inc., 200
West Street, New York, New York 10282. If your shares are held with certain banks, trust companies, brokers, dealers, investment advisers and other financial intermediaries (each, an &#147;Authorized Institution&#148;) and you would like to receive
a separate copy of future proxy statements, notices of internet availability of proxy materials, prospectuses or annual reports or you are now receiving multiple copies of these documents and would like to receive a single copy in the future, please
contact your Authorized Institution. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>IMPORTANT NOTICE REGARDING THE AVAILABILITY OF PROXY MATERIALS FOR THE ANNUAL MEETING TO BE HELD
ON FRIDAY, MAY&nbsp;17, 2019 </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This Proxy Statement is available online at <U>www.proxyvote.com</U> (please have the control number
found on your proxy card ready when you visit this website). </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Section</B><B></B><B>&nbsp;16(a) Beneficial Ownership Reporting Compliance</B> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Pursuant to Section&nbsp;16(a) of the Exchange Act, the Company&#146;s directors and executive officers and any persons holding more than 10%
of the Company&#146;s common stock are required to report their beneficial ownership and any changes therein to the SEC and the Company. Specific due dates for those reports have been established, and the Company is required to report in this proxy
statement any failure to file such reports by those due dates. Based on the Company&#146;s review of Forms 3, 4 and 5 filed by such persons and information provided by the Company&#146;s directors and executive officers, the Company believes that,
with respect to the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018, all Section&nbsp;16(a) filing requirements applicable to such persons were met in a timely manner. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>PROPOSAL 1 </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>ELECTION OF DIRECTORS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Board is divided into three classes with staggered three-year terms. At each annual meeting of Stockholders, the successors to the class
of directors whose term expires at such meeting will be elected to hold office for a term expiring at the annual meeting of Stockholders held in the third year following the year of their election. At the Meeting, you will be asked to elect two
Class&nbsp;II directors to serve until the 2022 annual meeting of stockholders or until his or her successor is duly elected and qualified or until his or her earlier death, resignation, removal or disqualification. In addition, the Board has
adopted policies which provide that (a)&nbsp;no director shall hold office for more than 15 years and (b)&nbsp;a director shall retire as of December 31st of the calendar year in which he or she reaches his or her 74th birthday, unless a waiver of
such requirement has been adopted by a majority of the other directors. These policies may be changed by the directors without a stockholder vote. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Information concerning the nominees and other relevant factors is provided below. Using the enclosed proxy card or voting by the Internet or
by telephone, a Stockholder may vote his or her shares for or against, or abstain from voting with respect to, the election of either nominee. If the enclosed proxy card is properly executed and received prior to the Meeting (and has not been
revoked) but no instructions are marked, the proxies will vote &#147;FOR&#148; the nominees. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Each of Ms.&nbsp;Kaysie Uniacke and
Mr.&nbsp;Jaime Ardila has consented to his or her nomination and has agreed to continue to serve if elected. If, at the time of the Meeting, for any reason, Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke or Mr.&nbsp;Ardila is not available for election or is not able to serve as
a director, the persons named as proxies intend to exercise their voting power in favor of such person as is nominated by the Board as a substitute. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>ON FEBRUARY&nbsp;27, 2019, THE BOARD, INCLUDING EACH OF THE INDEPENDENT DIRECTORS, UNANIMOUSLY RECOMMENDED THAT YOU VOTE &#147;FOR&#148;
EACH NOMINEE LISTED ABOVE. </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Information about the Nominees and Directors </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Set forth below are the names of the nominees for Class&nbsp;II directors, as well as each of the continuing directors, and their addresses,
ages, terms of office, principal occupations for at least the past five years and any other directorships they hold in companies which are subject to the reporting requirements of the Exchange Act or are registered as investment companies under the
1940 Act. Directors (including one of the nominees) who (1)&nbsp;are not deemed to be &#147;interested persons,&#148; as defined in the 1940 Act, of the Company, (2)&nbsp;meet the definition of &#147;independent directors&#148; under the corporate
governance standards of the NYSE and (3)&nbsp;meet the independence requirements of Section&nbsp;10A(m)(3) of the Exchange Act are referred to as &#147;Independent Directors.&#148; Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke (one of the nominees) is deemed to be an
&#147;interested person&#148; of the Company and is referred to as the &#147;Interested Director.&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Each of Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke or
Mr.&nbsp;Ardila has been nominated for election as a Class&nbsp;II director to serve until the 2022 annual meeting of stockholders. Neither of the nominees are being proposed for election pursuant to any agreement or understanding between such
nominee and the Company. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">5 </P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Each nominee and director may be contacted by writing to the nominee or director, c/o Goldman Sachs Asset

director&#146;s particular experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills is considered by the Board on an individual basis. Experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills common to all nominees and directors include the ability to
critically review, evaluate and discuss information provided to them and to interact effectively with the other directors and with representatives of GSAM and its affiliates, other service providers, legal counsel and the Company&#146;s independent
registered public accounting firm, the capacity to address financial and legal issues and exercise reasonable business judgment, and a commitment to the representation of the interests of the Company and the Stockholders. The Governance and
Nominating Committee&#146;s charter contains certain other factors that are considered by the Governance and Nominating Committee in identifying and evaluating potential nominees to serve as Independent Directors. Based on each nominee&#146;s
experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills, considered individually and with respect to the experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills of the other directors, the Board has concluded that each nominee should continue to serve as
a director. Below is a brief discussion of the experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills of each nominee, as well as of the continuing directors, that led the Board to conclude that such individual should serve as a director. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Class&nbsp;II Director Nominees </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Interested
Director </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Kaysie Uniacke</B>. Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke was elected as one of the Company&#146;s directors in January 2014. Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke
is the chair of the board of Goldman Sachs Asset Management International, serves on the boards of the Goldman Sachs Luxembourg and Dublin family of funds, several GSAM-managed pooled vehicles organized in the Cayman Islands, GS PMMC and GS MMLC and
is an advisory director to Group Inc. Previously, she was global chief operating officer of GSAM&#146;s portfolio management business until 2012 and served on the Investment Management Division Client and Business Standards Committee. Prior to this,
she was president of Goldman Sachs Trust, the GS mutual fund family, and was head of the Fiduciary Management business within Global Manager Strategies, responsible for business development and client service globally. Earlier in her career,
Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke managed GSAM&#146;s U.S. and Canadian Distribution groups. In that capacity, she was responsible for overseeing all North American institutional and third-party sales channels, marketing and client service functions, for which
client assets exceeded $200&nbsp;billion. Before that, Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke was head of GSAM&#146;s Global Cash Services business, where she was responsible for overseeing the management of assets exceeding $100&nbsp;billion. Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke worked at
Goldman Sachs from 1983 to 2012, where she was named managing director in 1997 and partner in 2002. Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke serves on the board of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Person-to-Person,</FONT></FONT> a <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-profit</FONT> organization that supports the working poor in lower Fairfield County, CT. Based on the foregoing, Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke is experienced with financial and investment matters. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Independent Directors </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Jaime
Ardila</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila was elected as one of the Company&#146;s directors in February 2016 and as Chairman of the Board in January 2018. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila is retired. He also serves as director and as Chairman of the Board of Directors of GS
PMMC. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila is a member of the Board of Directors of Accenture plc, a management consulting services company, where he serves as Chair of the Finance Committee and a member of the Audit Committee, and as a member of the Board of Directors
of Ecopetrol, an integrated oil company, where he serves as Chair of the Audit Committee and a member of the Business Committee and the Corporate Governance and </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">8 </P>

<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
Sustainability Committee. Previously, Mr.&nbsp;Ardila worked for 29 years at General Motors Company, an automobile manufacturer, where he held several senior management positions, most recently
as Executive Vice President of the company and President of General Motors&#146; South America region. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila joined General Motors in 1984. From 1996 to 1998, Mr.&nbsp;Ardila served as the managing director, Colombian Operations, of N M
Rothschild&nbsp;&amp; Sons Ltd, before rejoining General Motors in 1998. Based on the foregoing, Mr.&nbsp;Ardila is experienced with financial and investment matters. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Continuing Directors not up for <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">re-election</FONT> at the Meeting </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Independent Directors </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Ross J.
Kari</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Kari was elected as one of the Company&#146;s directors in August 2015. Mr.&nbsp;Kari is retired. He also serves on the Board of Directors of GS PMMC. Previously, Mr.&nbsp;Kari was Executive Vice President and Chief Financial
Officer of Federal Home Loan Mortgage Corporation (Freddie Mac), where he worked for four years. Previously, he held senior management positions at SAFECO Corporation, a personal insurance company, Federal Home Loan Bank of San Francisco, and Wells
Fargo&nbsp;&amp; Company, where he began his career and worked for 19 years. Mr.&nbsp;Kari also serves as a Director and a member of the Audit Committee and ALCO Chairman of Summit Bank. Based on the foregoing, Mr.&nbsp;Kari is experienced with
financial and investment matters. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Ann B. Lane</B>. Ms.&nbsp;Lane was elected as one of the Company&#146;s directors in February 2016.
Ms.&nbsp;Lane is retired. She also serves on the Board of Directors of GS PMMC. Ms.&nbsp;Lane was a Director of Dealertrack Technologies, Inc., an automotive software solutions and services company, from 2007 to 2015. Previously, she worked for five
years at JPMorgan Chase&nbsp;&amp; Co., a financial services company, as a Managing Director and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Co-Head</FONT> of Syndicated&nbsp;&amp; Leveraged Finance and Head of Loan Syndications Capital Markets. Prior to
joining JPMorgan Chase&nbsp;&amp; Co., Ms.&nbsp;Lane held several senior management positions at Citigroup, Inc., a financial services company, where she worked for 18 years. Based on the foregoing, Ms.&nbsp;Lane is experienced with financial and
investment matters. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Susan B. McGee</B>. Ms.&nbsp;McGee was elected to the Board on May&nbsp;1, 2018, with such election effective as
of June&nbsp;1, 2018. Ms.&nbsp;McGee is retired. She also serves on the Board of Directors of GS PMMC. Ms.&nbsp;McGee worked for 26 years at U.S. Global Investors, Inc., an investment management firm, until June 2018, during which time she held
several senior management positions, including President, General Counsel and Chief Compliance Officer. She has also been involved in the governance of the U.S. Global Investors Funds, serving as Vice President until June 2018. In addition,
Ms.&nbsp;McGee serves on the Board of Governors of the Investment Company Institute and as Chairperson of the Investment Company Institute Small Funds Committee. She is also a member of the Board of Directors of the San Antonio Sports Foundation, a <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">not-for-profit</FONT></FONT> organization. Based on the foregoing, Ms.&nbsp;McGee is experienced with financial and investment matters. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Compensation of Directors </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">From
January&nbsp;1, 2018 to December&nbsp;31, 2018, each Independent Director was compensated with a $100,000 annual fee for his or her services as director. In addition, the Chairman of the Board earned an additional annual fee of $33,000 and the
director designated as the &#147;audit committee financial expert,&#148; as defined in Item 407 of Regulation <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">S-K,</FONT> earned an additional annual fee of $11,000 for their additional services in these capacities.
The Independent Directors are reimbursed for travel and other expenses incurred in connection with attending Board and committee meetings. The Company may also pay the incidental costs of a director to attend training or other types of conferences
relating to the business development company (&#147;BDC&#148;) industry. In addition, the Company purchases directors&#146; and officers&#146; liability insurance on behalf of the directors. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">It is the responsibility of the Independent Directors to review their own compensation and recommend to all of the directors the appropriate
level of compensation. This level of compensation may be adjusted from time to time. In conducting their review, the Independent Directors use such information as they deem relevant, including compensation paid to directors of other BDCs of similar
size and the time and effort required of the directors in fulfilling their responsibilities to the Company. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">9 </P>

Directors for the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018. No compensation is paid by the Company to any Interested Director or executive officer of the Company. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(7)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Ms.&nbsp;Clark resigned from the Board effective as of the conclusion of the meeting of the Board held on
May&nbsp;1, 2018. Prior to her resignation, Ms.&nbsp;Clark was an Independent Director and was a member of the Audit Committee, the Governance and Nominating Committee, the Compensation Committee, the Compliance Committee and the Contract Review
Committee. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Board Composition and Leadership Structure </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company&#146;s business and affairs are managed under the direction of the Board. The Board consists of five members, four of whom are
Independent Directors. The Board elects the Company&#146;s officers, who serve at the discretion of the Board. The responsibilities of the Board include quarterly valuation of the Company&#146;s assets, corporate governance activities, oversight of
the Company&#146;s financing arrangements and oversight of its investment activities. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Board&#146;s role in the management of the
Company is one of oversight. Oversight of the Company&#146;s investment activities extends to oversight of the risk management processes employed by GSAM as part of its
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">day-to-day</FONT></FONT> management of the Company&#146;s investment activities. The Board reviews risk management processes at both regular and special Board meetings throughout the
year, consulting with appropriate representatives of GSAM as necessary and periodically requesting the production of risk management reports or presentations. The goal of the Board&#146;s risk oversight function is to ensure that the risks
associated with the Company&#146;s investment activities are accurately identified, thoroughly investigated and responsibly addressed. Stockholders should note, however, that the Board&#146;s oversight function cannot eliminate all risks or ensure
that particular events do not adversely affect the value of the Company&#146;s investments. The Board also has primary responsibility for the valuation of the Company&#146;s assets. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">10 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Board has established an Audit Committee, Governance and Nominating Committee, Compensation
Committee, Compliance Committee and Contract Review Committee. The scope of each committee&#146;s responsibilities is discussed in greater detail below. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Jaime Ardila, an Independent Director, serves as Chairman of the Board. The Board believes that it is in the best interests of the
Stockholders for Mr.&nbsp;Ardila to lead the Board because of his familiarity with the Company&#146;s portfolio companies, his broad corporate background and experience with financial and investment matters and his significant senior management
experience, as described above. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila generally acts as a liaison between management, officers and attorneys between meetings of the Board and presides over all executive sessions of the Independent Directors without management. The Board
believes that its leadership structure is appropriate because the structure allocates areas of responsibility among the individual directors and the committees in a manner that enhances effective oversight. The Board also believes that its size
creates an efficient corporate governance structure that provides opportunity for direct communication and interaction between management and the Board. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Board had nine formal meetings in 2018. Each continuing director that was a member of the Board during the fiscal year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2018 attended at least 75% of the aggregate number of meetings of the Board and of the respective committees during the periods that he or she served. To promote effectiveness of the Board, directors are strongly encouraged to
attend regularly scheduled Board meetings in person. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">None of the Company&#146;s directors attended the 2018 Annual Meeting of
Stockholders. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Committees of the Board </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Audit
Committee </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The current members of the Audit Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of
whom is an Independent Director. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila simultaneously serves on the audit committees of more than three public companies, and the Board has determined that his simultaneous service on the audit committees of other public companies does not
impair his ability to effectively serve on the Audit Committee. Mr.&nbsp;Kari serves as Chairman of the Audit Committee. The Board and the Audit Committee have determined that Mr.&nbsp;Kari is an &#147;audit committee financial expert,&#148; as
defined in Item 407 of Regulation <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">S-K.</FONT> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit Committee is responsible for overseeing matters
relating to the appointment and activities of the Company&#146;s auditors, audit plans and procedures, various accounting and financial reporting issues and changes in accounting policies, and reviewing the results and scope of the audit and other
services provided by the independent public accountants. The Audit Committee is also responsible for aiding the Board in fair value pricing debt and equity securities that are not publicly traded or for which current market values are not readily
available. The Audit Committee&#146;s charter is available on the Company&#146;s website (<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit Committee held seven formal meetings in 2018. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Governance and Nominating Committee </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The current members of the Governance and Nominating Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of
whom is an Independent Director. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila serves as the Chairman of the Governance and Nominating Committee. The Governance and Nominating Committee is responsible for identifying, researching and nominating Independent Directors for election
by the Stockholders, selecting nominees to fill vacancies on the Board or a committee of the Board, developing and recommending to the Board a set of corporate governance principles and overseeing the evaluation of the Board and management. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">11 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">All candidates nominated for an Independent Director position must meet applicable independence
requirements and have the capacity to address financial and legal issues and exercise reasonable business judgment. The Governance and Nominating Committee considers a variety of criteria in evaluating candidates (including candidates nominated by a
Stockholder), including (1)&nbsp;experience in business, financial or investment matters or in other fields of endeavor; (2)&nbsp;financial literacy and/or whether he or she is an &#147;audit committee financial expert,&#148; as defined in Item 407
of Regulation <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">S-K;</FONT> (3)&nbsp;reputation; (4) ability to attend scheduled Board and committee meetings; (5)&nbsp;general availability to attend to Board business on short notice; (6)&nbsp;actual or potential
business, family or other conflicts bearing on either the candidate&#146;s independence or the business of the Company; (7)&nbsp;length of potential service; (8)&nbsp;commitment to the representation of the interests of the Company and the
Stockholders; (9)&nbsp;commitment to maintaining and improving his or her skills and education; (10)&nbsp;experience in corporate governance and best business practices; and (11)&nbsp;the diversity that he or she would bring to the Board&#146;s
composition. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Governance and Nominating Committee considers nominees properly recommended by a Stockholder. The Company&#146;s bylaws
provide that for any nomination to be properly brought by a Stockholder for a meeting, such Stockholder must comply with advance notice requirements and provide the Company with certain information. Generally, to be timely, a Stockholder&#146;s
notice must be received at the Company&#146;s principal executive offices not less than 90 days nor more than 120 days prior to the first anniversary date of the immediately preceding annual meeting of Stockholders. The Company&#146;s bylaws further
provide that nominations of persons for election to the Board at a special meeting may be made only by or at the direction of the Board and, provided that the Board has determined that directors will be elected at the meeting, by a Stockholder who
is entitled to vote at the meeting and who has complied with the advance notice provisions of the bylaws. The Governance and Nominating Committee&#146;s charter is available on the Company&#146;s website
(<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Governance and Nominating Committee held four formal meetings in 2018. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Compensation Committee </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
current members of the Compensation Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of whom is an Independent Director. The Compensation Committee is responsible for determining, or recommending to the Board for
determination, the compensation, if any, of the Company&#146;s chief executive officer and all other executive officers. The Compensation Committee also assists the Board with matters related to compensation generally, except with respect to
compensation of the directors. As discussed in &#147;Compensation of Directors,&#148; below, it is the responsibility of the Independent Directors to review their own compensation and recommend to all of the directors the appropriate level of
compensation. As none of the Company&#146;s executive officers currently is compensated by the Company, the Compensation Committee does not produce and/or review a report on executive compensation practices. The Compensation Committee&#146;s charter
is available on the Company&#146;s website (<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Compensation Committee did not hold any
formal meetings in 2018. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Compliance Committee </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The current members of the Compliance Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of whom is an
Independent Director. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila serves as Chairman of the Compliance Committee. The Compliance Committee is responsible for overseeing the Company&#146;s compliance processes, and insofar as they relate to services provided to us, the
compliance processes of the investment adviser, underwriters (if any), administrator and transfer agent, except that compliance processes relating to the accounting and financial reporting processes and certain related matters are overseen by the
Audit Committee. In addition, the Compliance Committee provides assistance to the full Board with respect to compliance matters. The Compliance Committee&#146;s charter is available on the Company&#146;s website
(<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">12 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Compliance Committee held six formal meetings in 2018. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Contract Review Committee </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
current members of the Contract Review Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of whom is an Independent Director. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila serves as Chairman of the Contract Review Committee. The Contract Review
Committee is responsible for overseeing the processes of the Board for reviewing and monitoring performance under the Company&#146;s investment management, placement agent (if any), principal underwriting (if any) and certain other agreements with
GSAM and its affiliates. The Contract Review Committee also provides appropriate assistance to the Board in connection with the Board&#146;s approval, oversight and review of the Company&#146;s other service providers, including the Company&#146;s
custodian/accounting agent, transfer agent, printing firms, and professional firms (other than the Company&#146;s independent auditor, which is the responsibility of the Audit Committee). The Contract Review Committee&#146;s charter is available on
the Company&#146;s website (<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Contract Review Committee had one formal meeting in 2018.

<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Brendan McGovern</B>. Mr.&nbsp;McGovern was appointed as the Company&#146;s chief executive officer and president in March 2013.
Mr.&nbsp;McGovern heads GSAM&#146;s Private Credit Group, is the chief executive officer and president of GS PMMC and GS MMLC and also serves as <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-head</FONT> and senior portfolio manager of the GSAM Credit
Alternatives portfolio management team. He is also the Chair and a voting member of the Private Credit Group&#146;s Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. Mr.&nbsp;McGovern
joined the firm in 2006. Prior to joining the firm, Mr.&nbsp;McGovern served as a managing director in<B> </B>the Global Investment Group at Amaranth Advisors, where he <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-headed</FONT> the fund&#146;s private
placement efforts for both debt and equity linked products in the United States. He is also on the board of directors for the Oxalosis and Hyperoxaluria Foundation. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Jon Yoder</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Yoder was appointed as the Company&#146;s chief operating officer in March 2013. Mr.&nbsp;Yoder is the chief
operating officer of GS PMMC and GS MMLC and a member of GSAM&#146;s Private Credit Group with a focus on sourcing, structuring and executing privately negotiated debt financings. He is also a voting member of the Private Credit Group&#146;s
Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. Mr.&nbsp;Yoder joined the firm in 2005. Prior to joining the firm, he was a member of the mergers and acquisitions and private equity
groups at Paul, Weiss, Rifkind, Wharton&nbsp;&amp; Garrison, LLP. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">13 </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Jonathan Lamm</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Lamm was appointed as the Company&#146;s chief financial officer
and treasurer in March 2013. Mr.&nbsp;Lamm is also the chief financial officer and treasurer of GS PMMC and GS MMLC and chief operating officer of the GSAM Credit Alternatives portfolio management team, responsible for the operations of the
business, including business financials, infrastructure support, and IT project management, as well as the continuous improvement of the control environment. Mr.&nbsp;Lamm is secretary and a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-voting</FONT> member
of the Private Credit Group&#146;s Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. He joined the firm in 2002. Prior to joining the firm, Mr.&nbsp;Lamm worked in the securities audit
practice at Deloitte&nbsp;&amp; Touche LLP. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Maya Teufel</B>. Ms.&nbsp;Teufel was appointed as the Company&#146;s chief compliance
officer in December 2016. Ms.&nbsp;Teufel is also the chief compliance officer of GS PMMC and GS MMLC. Prior to joining GSAM in September 2016, she was, from November 2013 to August 2016, the General Counsel and Chief Compliance Officer of Emerging
Global Advisors, LLC (currently part of Ameriprise Financial). While at Emerging Global Advisors, Ms.&nbsp;Teufel also held the position of fund chief compliance officer from October 2015 to August 2016. Prior to joining Emerging Global Advisors,
she was, from July 2005 to November 2013, Vice President, Corporate Counsel at Prudential Insurance Company of America, a subsidiary of Prudential Financial Inc., an insurance and financial services company. Prior to Prudential, Ms.&nbsp;Teufel was
an associate in the mergers and acquisitions groups of Sullivan&nbsp;&amp; Cromwell LLP and Gibson, Dunn&nbsp;&amp; Crutcher LLP. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>David Yu</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Yu was appointed as an executive vice president and Head of Research of the Company in March 2013. Mr.&nbsp;Yu is
executive vice president and Head of Research of GS PMMC and GS MMLC and a member of the GSAM Private Credit Group with a focus on sourcing, structuring and executing privately negotiated debt financings and serves as its Head of Research.
Mr.&nbsp;Yu is a voting member of the Private Credit Group&#146;s Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. Mr.&nbsp;Yu joined the firm in 2006. Prior to joining the firm,
Mr.&nbsp;Yu was an associate in the Global Investments Group at Amaranth Advisors, where he similarly worked with public and private issuers to structure and execute debt and equity financings. Prior to joining Amaranth, he worked in the Leveraged
Finance and Sponsor Coverage Group at CIBC World Markets. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Michael Mastropaolo</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Mastropaolo was appointed as an executive
vice president of the Company in February 2019. Mr.&nbsp;Mastropaolo is executive vice president of GS PMMC and GS MMLC and a member of the GSAM Credit Alternatives team with a focus on sourcing, structuring and executing privately negotiated debt
financings. He is also a voting member of the Private Credit Group&#146;s Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. Mr.&nbsp;Mastropaolo joined the firm in 2016. Prior to joining
the firm, Mr.&nbsp;Mastropaolo was a director at Golub Capital where he originated and managed middle market debt and equity investments. Mr.&nbsp;Mastropaolo started his career at General Electric in the Investment Analyst training program at GE
Capital. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Jordan Walter</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Walter was appointed as an executive vice president of the Company in February 2018.
Mr.&nbsp;Walter is executive vice president of GS PMMC and GS MMLC and a member of the GSAM Credit<B> </B>Alternatives team with a focus on sourcing, structuring and executing privately negotiated debt financings. He is also a voting member of the
Private Credit Group&#146;s Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. Mr.&nbsp;Walter joined the firm in 2014. Prior to joining the firm, Mr.&nbsp;Walter was a vice president at
MCG Capital where he originated and managed middle market debt and equity investments. Prior to joining MCG Capital, Mr.&nbsp;Walter was in the Financial Management Program at General Electric. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Carmine Rossetti</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Rossetti was appointed as principal accounting officer of the Company in May 2017. Mr.&nbsp;Rossetti is also
the principal accounting officer of GS PMMC and GS MMLC and head of the GSAM Hedge Fund and BDC Fund Controller teams. Mr.&nbsp;Rossetti is responsible for fund accounting and financial reporting oversight as well as the continuous improvement of
the control environment. Mr.&nbsp;Rossetti joined Goldman Sachs in 2004. Prior to joining Goldman Sachs, he worked in the audit practice at Ernst&nbsp;&amp; Young LLP. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">14 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Certain Relationships and Related Party Transactions </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Investment Management Agreement </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company is party to an investment management agreement, pursuant to which the Company pays GSAM, a wholly owned subsidiary of Group Inc., a
fee for investment management services consisting of a management fee based on the Company&#146;s gross assets (excluding cash and cash equivalents but including assets purchased with borrowed amounts) and an incentive fee based on the performance
of the Company&#146;s investments. Certain of the Company&#146;s officers are also officers and employees of GSAM. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2018, the management fee was calculated at (i)&nbsp;an annual rate of 1.50% (0.375% per quarter) (the &#147;Original Rate&#148;) through June&nbsp;14, 2018 and (ii)&nbsp;an annual rate of 1.00% (0.25% per quarter) (the &#147;New
Rate&#148;) thereafter, in each case, of the average value of the Company&#146;s gross assets at the end of each of the two most recently completed calendar quarters. The management fee for any partial quarter (including any quarter during which
both the Original Rate and the New Rate were in effect) was prorated based on the actual number of days elapsed relative to the total number of days in such calendar quarter. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018, the Company paid GSAM a total of $34.35&nbsp;million in fees (excluding fees that are accrued but
not paid) pursuant to the investment management agreement, which consisted of $17.18&nbsp;million in management fees and $17.17&nbsp;million in incentive fees. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>License Agreement </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company is
party to a license agreement with an affiliate of Goldman Sachs pursuant to which the Company has been granted a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-exclusive,</FONT> royalty-free license to use the &#147;Goldman Sachs&#148; name. Under this
agreement, the Company does not have a right to use the Goldman Sachs name if GSAM or another affiliate of Goldman Sachs is not the Company&#146;s investment adviser or if the Company&#146;s continued use of such license results in a violation of
applicable law, results in a regulatory burden or has adverse regulatory consequences. Other than with respect to this limited license, the Company has no legal right to the &#147;Goldman Sachs&#148; name. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Co-Investment</FONT> Opportunities </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company has in the past <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-invested,</FONT> and in the future may
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-invest,</FONT> on a concurrent basis with other funds managed by GSAM and its affiliates, but not if such <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-investment</FONT> is impermissible under existing regulatory guidance,
applicable regulations or GSAM&#146;s allocation procedures. Certain types of negotiated <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-investments</FONT> may be made only if the Company receives an order from the SEC permitting the Company to do so. On
January&nbsp;4, 2017, the SEC granted the Company, GS PMMC and GS MMLC, as well as certain other funds managed by GSAM in the future, the exemptive relief to make negotiated <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-investments,</FONT> subject to certain
terms and conditions in the exemptive relief. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Related Party Transaction Review Policy </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit Committee conducts quarterly reviews of any potential related party transactions brought to its attention and, during these reviews,
it also considers any conflicts of interest brought to its attention pursuant to the Company&#146;s Code of Ethics. Each of the Company&#146;s directors and executive officers is instructed and periodically reminded to inform GSAM Compliance of any
potential related party transactions. In addition, each such director and executive officer completes a questionnaire on an annual basis designed to elicit information about any potential related party transactions. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">15 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>PROPOSAL 2 </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>RATIFICATION OF SELECTION OF INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">At a meeting of the Board held on December&nbsp;6, 2018, the Audit Committee selected and recommended, and the Board, including a majority of
the Independent Directors approved, the selection of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP to act as the independent registered public accounting firm for the Company for the fiscal year ending December&nbsp;31, 2019. This selection is presented for
ratification by the Stockholders. If the Stockholders fail to ratify the selection of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP to serve as the independent registered public accounting firm for the year ending December&nbsp;31, 2019, the Audit Committee and the
Board will reconsider the continued retention of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Representatives of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP are expected
to be available telephonically during the Meeting and will be available to respond to appropriate questions from Stockholders if necessary. Representatives of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP will be given the opportunity to make statements at the
Meeting, if they so desire. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Audit Fees </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The aggregate audit fees billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2018 and December&nbsp;31, 2017 were
$808,500 and $761,500, respectively. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Fees included in the audit fees category are those associated with the annual audits of financial
statements, review of the financial statements included in the Company&#146;s Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-Qs</FONT> and services that are normally provided in connection with statutory and regulatory filings. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Audit-Related Fees </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">No
audit-related fees were billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2018 and December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Audit-related fees are for any services rendered to the Company that are reasonably related to the performance of the audits or reviews of the
Company&#146;s financial statements (but not reported as audit fees above). These services include attestation services that are not required by statute or regulation and consultations concerning financial accounting and reporting standards. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Tax Fees </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The aggregate fees
billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP for services rendered to the Company for tax compliance, tax advice and tax planning for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2018 and December&nbsp;31, 2017 were $58,750 and $43,750, respectively. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Fees included in the tax fees category comprise all services performed by professional staff in the independent registered public
accountant&#146;s tax division except those services related to the audits. This category comprises fees for tax compliance services provided in connection with the preparation and review of the Company&#146;s tax returns. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>All Other Fees </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">No fees were
billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP for products and services provided to the Company, other than the services reported in &#147;Audit Fees,&#148; &#147;Audit Related Fees,&#148; and &#147;Tax Fees&#148; above, for the years ended December&nbsp;31,
2018 and December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">16 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Aggregate <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-Audit</FONT> Fees </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The aggregate <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-audit</FONT> fees billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP to GSAM, and any entity controlling,
controlled by, or under common control with, GSAM, that provides ongoing services to the Company, for engagements directly related to the Company&#146;s operations and financial reporting, for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2018 and
December&nbsp;31, 2017, were $1,166,488 and $1,133,433, respectively. These amounts represent fees PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP billed to GSAM for services related to the Statement on Standards for Attestation Engagements No.&nbsp;18 report. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Pre-Approval</FONT> of Audit and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-Audit</FONT> Services Provided to the Company
</B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-Audit</FONT> Services <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Pre-Approval</FONT> Policy
(the &#147;Policy&#148;) adopted by the Audit Committee sets forth the procedures and the conditions pursuant to which services performed by an independent auditor for the Company may be <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approved.</FONT> Services
may be <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approved</FONT> specifically by the Audit Committee as a whole or, in certain circumstances, by the Audit Committee Chairman, or by such other members of the Audit Committee who may be granted authority by
the Audit Committee to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approve</FONT> services on its behalf. In addition, subject to specified cost limitations, certain services may be <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approved</FONT> under the provisions
of the Policy. The Policy provides that the Audit Committee will consider whether the services provided by an independent auditor are consistent with the SEC&#146;s rules on auditor independence. The Policy provides for periodic review and <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approval</FONT> by the Audit Committee of the services that may be provided by the independent auditor. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>De Minimis Waiver</I>. The <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approval</FONT> requirements of the Policy may be waived with respect to
the provision of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-audit</FONT> services that are permissible for an independent auditor to perform, provided (1)&nbsp;the aggregate amount of all such services provided constitutes no more than five percent of the
total amount of revenues subject to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approval</FONT> that was paid to the independent auditors during the fiscal year in which the services are provided; (2)&nbsp;such services were not recognized by the Company
at the time of the engagement to be <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-audit</FONT> services; and (3)&nbsp;such services are promptly brought to the attention of the Audit Committee and approved prior to the completion of the audit by the Audit
Committee or by one or more members of the Audit Committee to whom authority to grant such approvals has been delegated by the Audit Committee, pursuant to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approval</FONT> provisions of the Policy. The Audit
Committee did not approve any of the audit, audit-related, tax, or other <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-audit</FONT> fees described above pursuant to the &#147;<I>de minimis </I>exceptions&#148; set forth in
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Rule&nbsp;2-01(c)(7)(i)(C)</FONT> and Rule <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-01(c)(7)(ii)</FONT> of Regulation <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">S-X.</FONT> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Pre-Approval</FONT> of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-Audit</FONT> Services Provided to GSAM.
</I>The Policy provides that, in addition to requiring <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approval</FONT> of audit and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-audit</FONT> services provided to the Company, the Audit Committee will <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-approve</FONT> those <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-audit</FONT> services provided to GSAM (and entities controlling, controlled by or under common control with GSAM that provide ongoing services to the Company)
where the engagement relates directly to the operations or financial reporting of the Company.<I> </I>The Audit Committee has considered these fees and the nature of the services rendered, and has concluded that they are compatible with maintaining
the independence of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. Except as described above, PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP did not provide any audit services, audit-related services, tax services or other <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-audit</FONT> services to
GSAM or any entity controlling, controlled by or under common control with GSAM that provides ongoing services to the Company that the Audit Committee was required to approve pursuant to Rule <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-01(c)(7)(ii)</FONT> of
Regulation <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">S-X.</FONT> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>ON FEBRUARY&nbsp;27, 2019, THE BOARD, INCLUDING EACH OF THE INDEPENDENT
DIRECTORS, UNANIMOUSLY RECOMMENDED THAT YOU VOTE &#147;FOR&#148; THE RATIFICATION OF&nbsp;PRICEWATERHOUSECOOPERS LLP AS INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING&nbsp;FIRM TO THE COMPANY FOR THE FISCAL YEAR ENDING DECEMBER&nbsp;31, 2019. </B></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">17 </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B><I>Audit Committee Report
</I></B><B><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(1)</SUP></B> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following is the report of the Audit Committee of Goldman
Sachs BDC, Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;) with respect to the Company&#146;s audited financial statements for the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018 (the &#147;Audited Financial Statements&#148;). </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit Committee has: (a)&nbsp;reviewed and discussed the Audited Financial Statements with the management of the Company;
(b)&nbsp;discussed with the independent auditor the matters required to be discussed by Auditing Standard 1301 (Communications with Audit Committees), as adopted by the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (&#147;PCAOB&#148;); and
(c)&nbsp;received the written disclosures and the letter from the independent auditor required by applicable requirements of the PCAOB Ethics and Independence Rule 3526 regarding the independent auditor&#146;s communications with the Audit Committee
concerning independence, and has discussed with the independent auditor the auditor&#146;s independence. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The members of the Audit
Committee are not, and do not represent themselves to be, professionally engaged in the practice of auditing or accounting and are not employed by the Company for accounting, financial management or internal control purposes. Moreover, the Audit
Committee relies on and makes no independent verification of the facts presented to it or representations made by management or the Company&#146;s independent auditor. Accordingly, the Audit Committee&#146;s oversight does not provide an independent
basis to determine that management has maintained appropriate accounting and/or financial reporting principles and policies, or internal controls and procedures designed to assure compliance with accounting standards and applicable laws and
regulations. Furthermore, the Audit Committee&#146;s considerations and discussions referred to above do not provide assurance that the audit of the Company&#146;s financial statements has been carried out in accordance with the standards of the
PCAOB or that the financial statements are presented in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Based on its
consideration of the Audited Financial Statements and the discussions referred to above with management and the Company&#146;s independent auditor, and subject to the limitations on the responsibilities and role of the Audit Committee set forth in
the charter and those discussed above, the Audit Committee recommended to the Board of Directors that the Audited Financial Statements be accepted by the Board of Directors and included in the Company&#146;s Annual Report on Form <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-K</FONT> for the last fiscal year for filing with the SEC. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">February&nbsp;27, 2019 </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>The Audit Committee </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Ross
